Nano Energy 76 (2020) 104997 7 superior cycling performance at 1200 mA g   1. Table S5 summarizes the comparison of our electrochemical testing results with latest reports in literature. The best rate performance and outstanding overall electro chemical properties of NAFMO-LN electrode demonstrate a potential competitive advantage to the general P2 cathodes. Fig. 5. (a) In-situ synchrotron XRD patterns of Na 0.67 Al 0.1 Fe 0.05 Mn 0.85 O 2 -LN material during first charge/discharge process at 24 mA g   1 in the voltage range of 2–4 V. Black asterisks (*) represent peaks from Al window and the electrode phases are shown at the right of each pattern. (b) Ex-situ 23 Na NMR spectra of Na 0.67 Al 0.1 Fe 0.05 Mn 0.85 O 2 -LN material during the initial charge-discharge cycles. The cycling curves are shown at the left of each spectrum. Na contents are rep resented by x and shown on the left of each spectrum. X. Liu et al. Nano Energy 76 (2020) 104997 8 3.3. Long-range and local structural transformations during (De) Sodiation processes In-situ synchrotron XRD was employed to track the long-range structural transformations of NAFMO-LN electrode induced by the (de)intercalation of Na þ at a rate current of 24 mA g   1. As shown in Fig. 5 a, the XRD patterns have been divided into four stages to clarify the structure evolution process more clearly. The (002), (110), (112), (113) and (114) peaks are retained during the whole process, corresponding to a quasi-solid-solution reaction rather than typically multiple-phases transition reaction according to the previous reports [ 45,46 ]. As indi cated above, the prepared electrode is assigned to a P2 0 I phase, which exhibits a slight orthorhombic distortion from P2 phase. At the begin ning of charge process, the (020) peak reduces in intensity and shifts to higher angle, corresponding to the decrease of distortion degree, and a P2 phase is formed at x 1⁄4 0.40. Afterwards, a board peak is observed at the higher diffraction angle of 9 � at the end of charge process, owing to the formation of small amount of O-type stacking in the P2 structure. As reported by Bruce ’ s group, this process should be indicated as a “ Z ” phase evolved by the intergrowth mechanism, which have been mentioned in many P2 compounds, especially those containing Fe 3 þ [ 35, 47, 48 ]. The formation of “ Z ” phase is more moderate than O2 phase at high voltage, as the lattice parameter changes are smaller in magni tude and less abrupt, leading to a stable structure and better capacity retention [ 49 ]. The structural evolution is highly reversible during discharge. Of note, the (002), (110), (112), (113) and (114) peaks of P2 phase maintain in the rest of the discharge process, rather than replaced by that of typical P2 ’ phase with high degree of orthorhombic distortion (denoted as P2 ’ II). As the x equals 0.79, the characteristic signals of P2 ’ II phase are presented in both in-situ XRD and ss-NMR ( Fig. 5 b) results. However, such a moderate phase transition also makes it hard to distinguish between the P2 ’ I and P2 ’ II phase from in-situ XRD results. As shown in Fig. 5 b, the local environment information of the elec trode materials can be observed through 23 Na MAS NMR spectra, since Na þ directly participates in the electrochemical reaction in NIBs. 23 Na 1D slices were extracted from²D projection-MATPASS (pj-MATPASS) NMR spectra to eliminate the sideband signals [ 50 ]. Consistent with the powder sample, the ss-NMR spectrum of NAFMO-LN pristine electrode also shows the resonance signals at ~1250 ppm and ~0 ppm, rather than monoclinic and hydrated phases that usually occur during elec trode prepared process, suggesting that P2 ’ I phase is stable and structural transitions do not occur during electrode preparing procedure [ 34, 51 ]. During initial charge and discharge processes, the chemical shift of the signal moves to the high and low value gradually, corre spongding to the increase and decrease of the Mn ions average valence, respectively. The local structural evolution is in good agreement with the results of in situ XRD. When the x 1⁄4 0.32, the amount of local environment significantly increases because of the glide of MnO 2 layers, a wide peak at ~1100 ppm emerges, corresponding to the “ Z ” phase. Besides, the P2 phase signal can also be observed at the high voltage and decrease in intensity with “ Z ” phase emerging, which further proves the formation of “ Z ” phase is an intermediate and moderate process evolving intergrowth of P2 and O2 phases. The local structure is also highly reversible in discharge process. In x 1⁄4 0.78, the characteristic signal of P2 ’ II phase appears at ~850 ppm, which are clearly distin guished from the signal of P2 ’ I phase. Besides, the P2 ’ II phase signal signal of P2 ’ II phase appears at ~850 ppm, which are clearly distin guished from the signal of P2 ’ I phase. Besides, the P2 ’ II phase signal of NAFMO-LN sample is much broader than that of non-doped P2 0 -Na 0.67 MnO 2 materials while similar to the stable P2 - Na 0.67 Mg 0.1 Mn 0.9 O 2 and P2 - Na 0.67 Al 0.1 Mn 0.9 O 2 materials in previ ous works [ 34, 39 ], corresponding to a much more moderate structure transition and thus better cycle performance. 3.4. Effects of various doping elements on structural and electrochemical properties of materials In order to give some illustration on the significance of the work, the Mn ions average valence of layered oxide materias have been adjusted by introducting different valence doping element, e.g. the introduction of Li þ is expected to rise 3 folds molar equivalents of Mn 3 þ to Mn 4 þ, and 2 folds for Mg 2 þ and equal amount for Al 3 þ. Therefore, Na 0.67 M 0.1 Mn 0.9 O 2 (M 1⁄4 Li þ, Mg 2 þ, Al 3 þ ) and non-doped materials were also prepared via the same synthesis process to further reveal the rela tionship between the Mn oxidation state, structure and electrochemical properties. The longand short-range structural information are showed in Fig. 6. The obvious orthorhombic distortion of P2 phase can been found in non-doped NMO-QU/-LN and Al 3 þ -doped NAMO-LN samples with exhibiting the characteristic signals of P2 ’ phase in both XRD patterns and ss-NMR spectra. Also, orthorhombic distortion is observed for Mg 2 þ -doped NMMO-LN sample, just like the above results of NAFMO-LN sample. While the Li þ -doped NLMO samples do not show any distortion in both longand short-structure by each cooling treat ment. Besides, the full width at half maximum of P2 phase also become narrow continuously with the faster cooling treatment for each prepared material. The above results indicate that the orthorhombic distortion tends to exist in the materials with low theoretical manganese valence and TM vacancies can be suppressed for P2 type Na 0.67 M x Mn 1-x O 2 by the faster cooling treatment, and then exhibiting a more uniform local environment. A comparison of the electrochemical performance of non-doped and doped Na 0.67 M x Mn 1-x O 2 materials (Li þ, Mg 2 þ, Al 3 þ and Fe 3 þ ) prepared by NC, QU and LN methods is shown in Fig. 6 a - e. The initial charge and discharge capacities of all prepared materials increase significantly with the accelerating cooling rate, and the maximum capacity is obtained by liquid N 2 quenching (LN) treatment for all samples, demonstrating that the rapid cooling treatment can eliminate Mn vacancies, increase redox centers, and effectively improve the capacity of P2 type Na 0.67 M x Mn 1x O 2. Moreover, Fig. 7 f and S13 show that the cycle stablity of Na 0.67 M x Mn 1-x O 2 materials is highly related to the Mn ions average valence in the materials except for NAFMO-LN sample, which exhibits optimal electrochemical performance through the synergy effect of Al and Fe co-doping [ 32, 33 ]. The lower Mn ions average valence causes more severe orthorhombic distortion in Na 0.67 M x Mn 1-x O 2 and thus being detrimental to cyclability, e.g. the highest specific capacity (215 mAh g   1, 2–4 V) but lowest capacity retention of non-doped NMO-LN (Mn þ 3.33, δ 1⁄4 5.59%) sample, exhibiting many small plateau in galva nostatic charge-discharge curves. In contrast, the doped samples exhibit much smoother charge-discharge profiles, which evidences that the introduction of non-electrochemically active element disrupt the TM ordering in the TM layers and hamper Na þ -vacancy ordering during cycling [ 13 ]. The 10 mol% of Li-doping material presents a pure P2 phase without any lattice distortion and a stable cycling performance. However, even with liquid N 2 quenched treatment, NLMO-LN (Mn þ 3.59, δ 1⁄4 0%) sample only delivers specific capacity of 130 mAh g   1. There However, even with liquid N 2 quenched treatment, NLMO-LN (Mn þ 3.59, δ 1⁄4 0%) sample only delivers specific capacity of 130 mAh g   1. There fore, a rational element substitution should be implemented to mitigate Jahn-Teller effect and make a balance bewteen the capacity and cycle stablity to achieve superior electrochemical performance. Thus, the optimal co-doped NAFMO-LN material, with moderate initial Mn ions valence (Mn þ 3.39 ) and slight distortion ( δ 1⁄4 2.91%), shows not only an outstanding capacity of 202 mAh g   1 at voltage range of 2–4 V, but also a satifactory cyclability of 90.4% after 30 cycles at 12 mA g   1. 4. Conclusion In summary, our comparative results obtained in Na cells of nondoped and doped Na 0.67 M x Mn 1-x O 2 materials with Li þ, Mg 2 þ, Al 3 þ and Fe 3 þ prepared via different cooling processes is verified by using the combination of in-situ synchrotron XRD, TOF PND and ss-NMR mea surements. They reveal that a simple liquid N 2 quenching treatment X. Liu et al. Nano Energy 76 (2020) 104997 9 Fig. 6. (a - d) Powder XRD and (e - h) ss-NMR spectra of Li þ -doped, Mg 2 þ -doped, Al 3 þ -doped and non-doped Na 0.67 MnO 2 materials with different cooling treatment. Na 0.67 Li 0.1 Mn 0.9 O 2, Na 0.67 Mg 0.1 Mn 0.9 O 2, Na 0.67 Al 0.1 Mn 0.9 O 2 and Na 0.67 MnO 2 are denoted as NLMO, NMMO, NAMO and NMO, respectively. The spinning sideband signal and the characteristic signal of orthorhombic distortion are marked with “ * “ and ” z “, respectively. X. Liu et al. Nano Energy 76 (2020) 104997 10 could be regarded as a genaral synergetic strategy to control the for mation of vacancy in TM layers and thus to enhance Mn 4 þ /Mn 3 þ redox center. Consequently, the deliverable capacity of all the Mn-based Na 0.67 M x Mn 1-x O 2 materials can be signifcantly improved below 4.0 V, eliminating the factors responsible of capacity dacay such as electrolyte decomposition, structural collapse and oxygen loss at high voltgate. The ss-NMR, GITT and direct-current polarization results demonstrate the highest Na þ mobility and electronic conductivity for the liquid N 2 quenching sample, among the three different cooling rate samples. Moreover, we introduced Al and Fe, the top two earth abundance metal elements into TM layers to form the cost-effective Na 0.67 Al 0.1 Fe 0.05 Mn 0.85 O 2 compound. After liquid N 2 quenching, the slightly dis torted Na 0.67 Al 0.1 Fe 0.05 Mn 0.85 O 2 delivers a remarkable capacity of 202 and 246 mAh g   1 within 2.0–4.0 V and 1.5–4.5 V, respectively. Even with 100 times higher current density (1200 mA g   1 ), the specific capacity remains up to 122 mAh g   1 over 600 cycles with 81% capacity retention, indicating exceptional rate and power capabilities with excellent cycling stability. The outstanding overall performance of Na 0.67 Al 0.1 Fe 0.05 Mn 0.2 material demonstrated the synergetic strategy of liquid N 2 quenching treatment and rational element substitution, which can be used as a general guide for the further development of high ca pacity, high power and stable cycling materials, especially for Mn-based layered electrodes in NIBs. Introduction For the sake of realizing the sustainable development of human society, the employment of clean energy instead of fossil fuel has become the req uire ment of contempor ary society. In the w ake of the rapidl y gro wing demand for large-scale energy stor age syst ems, electric vehicles, smart grids, and recharg eable batt eries with high energy and po wer density are the most sensible choice for v arious energy stor age technologies [1–3]. Electrochemical energy stor age repr esented by lithium-ion batteries has become the main energy stor age method now. How ever, lithium reserv es are not abundant, and the increasing cost re strict its e xte nsiv e and large-scale appli cation. By contrast, sodium is currentl y the fourth-largest element in the earth’s crust, and it is cheap. Therefor e, sodium ion batt eries are e xpect ed to re place lithium ion batt eries in some specific energy stor age market s, which can alleviate the shortage of lithium re sources to a certain e xtent [4,5]. Both Li and Na are alkali metals, the ionic radi us of Na + is larger than Li + (1 .02 vs 0.7 6) [6–8]. R ecentl y, P2-type materials ha ve attract ed considerable inter est because of their e x cellent cy cling stability and rat e capacity [9, 1 0]. The lay ered P2 phase structure Na x MO 2 with high specific capacity has re ceiv ed widespread atten tion due to its attr activ e price combined with envir onmental friendliness [1 1]. How ever, the e xpected electrochemical perfor mance for P2-Na x MO 2 is often unsatisfactory. This is mainly due to the serious Jahn-T eller effect re lated to the Mn 3+ /Mn 4+ redo x couple, causing the P2-P2' phase tran sition [1 2] ther eby affecting Na + MO 2 is often unsatisfactory. This is mainly due to the serious Jahn-T eller effect re lated to the Mn 3+ /Mn 4+ redo x couple, causing the P2-P2' phase tran sition [1 2] ther eby affecting Na + tran sport kinetics [1 3]. A prime symbol ( ′ ) is used to indicate inplane distortion of the he xagonal lattice in the crystal structure, such as for P2-type [1 4]. The distortion reduces the Na + mobility and further leads to structural collapse during repeat ed cy cles. Therefor e, further processing and optimization of structur al stability are of great concern. Element doping is gener ally considered to be an ef fectiv e measure to re duce the deformation of transition metal lay er spacing and thus impro ve the re versibility of the structure. Where fore, understanding the effect of different doping elements is key to further develop and optimize Na x MO 2 cathodes for NIBs. For in stance, Ni is used to pro viding high voltag e to elev ate the a ver age discharge voltag e [1 4–1 7]. Fe doping suppresses minor structur al tran sitions during cy cling and Fe 3+ /Fe 4+ redo x couple pr ovides higher wor king pot ential [1 8]. Mg can stabilize the structur e by suppressing structural deformation to the orthogon al phase, but the https ://doi.org/1 0. 1 0 1 6/j.jallcom.2022. 1 65569 0925–8388/© 2022 Published by Elsevier B.V. ]] ]] ]]]]]] ⁎ Corresponding author at: Xi'an K ey Laborat ory of Clean Energy, Xi’an U niver sity of Archit ecture and T echnology, 7 1 0 055 Xi’an, PR China E-mail address: juan w ang@xauat.edu.cn (J. W ang). Journal of Alloys and Compounds 9 1 8 (2022) 1 65569 incorporation of inactiv e Mg will affect the activ ity of Mn 3+ / Mn 4+ [1 9–2 1]. How ever, Co is an inter esting alternati ve, which can be inv olv ed in redo x re actions in parallel with Mn during the cy cle. W ang et al. [22] ha ve successfull y synthesized P2 - Na 2/3 Mn y Co 1-y O 2 by con ventional solid state reaction. How ever, diffusion of Na + has not been adeq uatel y studied. Although P2-Na 0.67 Co 0.5 Mn 0.5 O 2 pr epared by Zhu et al. It w as pointe d out that the electrochemistry performance of the flake structur e materia l doped w as not outstanding. K onaro v et al. [25] mainly conducted w ork on the P2-P2' phase transition. But we pro ve that Co has an adv antage ous inhibitory effect on the P2-P2' phase tran sition besides the impro vement of Na + diffusion used by lattice paramet er changes and DFT. It is w orth mentioning that, the flake structure with an ob vious and uniform size prepar ed by the h ydro thermal method can promo te the diffusion of Na + and accel erat e the reaction rat e. As far as w e know, the influence of Co on Na 0.67 MnO 2 is considered for the first time comprehensi vel y and profoundl y from the aspects of morphology, crystal structure, and electronic structur e. In addition, although Co has a prominent effect on the impro vement of electrochemical performance, the price of Co is relati vel y high. Using of less stoich iometric ratio is also a promi nent factor that must be taken into consideration. Here, Na 0.67 Mn 1-x Co x O 2 (x = 0,0. 1 ,0.2) prepar ed by h ydr othermal method ha ve been studied as cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries. The Co 3+ and Mn 4+ wer e stable and random ly distributed in the trans ition metal lay er. Most importantly, the incorporation of Co can effectiv ely low er the Mn 3+ with the JahnT eller effect and lessen the irrev ersible distortion of P2-P2 ́ materia l. Furt hermore, the particles of NCM2 prepar ed by the h ydro thermal method ha ve high purity, and uniform particle size, which wer e conduciv e to the diffusion of Na + and accelerat e the reaction rat e. In this paper, we comprehend the positiv e role of Co doping in the Na 0.67 MnO 2 cathode using a series of electrochemical analy sis methods. 2. Experiment section All chemicals used are re ceiv ed from Sigma-Aldrich without further purification. The precursor w as synthesized by using am monium bicarbonate (NH 4 HCO 3 ) as a precipitant assisted thr ough the h ydro thermal method. First, a certain stoichiometric solution of cobalt acetate and manganese acetate with a ratio of 1/1 0:9/1 0 w as added into 30 mL deionized w ater and stirred to form a uniform solution, then a certain amount of NH 4 HCO 3 w as added into the abov e solution for uniform stirring. The resulting solution w as put into the react or. Set the temper atur e of the chemical re action. After natural cooling, the h ydro thermal reaction product w as filte red and then w ashed three times. Vacuum drying at 80 °C for 24 h, the precursor w as obtained and calcined at 50 0 °C for 6 h. After natural cooling, the prec ursor and e x cess 5 %mol of anh ydr ous sodium car bonate w ere fully ground in an agate mortar and calcined at 90 0 °C for 1 0 h, Na 0.67 Co 0. 1 Mn 0.9 O 2 (N CM1) w as obtained, and Na 0.67 Co 0.2 Mn 0.8 O 2 (NCM2) and Na 0.67 MnO 2 (NM) wer e prepar ed with the same method described abov e. The prepar ation diagram is shown in Fig. 1. 2. 1. Materials char acterization The phase composition of the composites w as analy zed by X -ra y powder diffr actometry (XRD-70 0) made by Shimadzu shown in Fig. 1. 2. 1. Materials char acterization The phase composition of the composites w as analy zed by X -ra y powder diffr actometry (XRD-70 0) made by Shimadzu Manufacturing Institute in Japan. Sodium metal w as applied to the counter electrode, where as har d carbon w as used as anode for the full cell. 1 M NaPF 6 in an EC/DEC (1:1 v/v) w as used as electrol yte. A glass fiber (GF/D) w as served as a separat or. The mass loading of activ e materia l w as around 1 .2 mg/cm². The CR2032 cell w as assembled in an Ar -filled glov e bo x. R esults and discussion Examination of the XRD patterns demonstrat es that single-phase materia ls wer e obtained for all the studied compositions. This w as confirmed by Rietve ld re finement using the Full prof suite Progr am ( Fig. 2 a-c). The materia ls show ed a P2-type structure, crystallized in the P63/mmc space gr oup. The diffraction peaks of all the samples are consistent with the standard card PDF2 7–05 7 1 [26]. Furthermor e, no impurity peak is observed, which indicates that Co is well in corporat ed into the crystal lattice. The unit cell paramet ers a of Co doped materials are decreased with the augment of Co content but enlarges d spacing ( T able S1 ). The Na-O bond of the Co-doped ma teri al increases but the TM-O and O-O bonds are shortened, which makes the insertion and de-insertion of Na + diffusion easier. The shorte ning of the TM-O bond and O-O bond is beneficial to the structur al stability of P2-type materials [2 7]. Fig. 2 d show s the shift of the base peak to w ards left as the cobalt content impro vement, re vealing the shrinkage of the TMO 2. There is the lattice structure of lay ered P2 - Na 2/3 Mn 1-x Co x O 2 (x = 0,0. 1 ,0.2) ( Fig. 2 d). The two tran sition metals ( Co/Mn ) are randoml y distribut ed in the MO2 lay er on account of the condition that Co 3+ (0.545 Å), Co 4+ (0.53 Å), and Mn 4+ (0.53 Å) ha ve similar ion radii [28,29]. It can be seen from ( T able S2–4) that Co is smoothl y doped in the transition metal lay er. In P2 type structure, sodium ions at the prism site are supposed to pass thr ough the cente r of a relati vel y wide plane q uadrilate ral con tributing P2 diffusion barrier that is relati vel y low, which can show e x cellent electroc hemical performance [30,3 1]. As shown in Fig. 3 a-b, the XRD test w as performed on the NM and NCM2 after the 1 0th, 50th, and 1 0 0th cy cles. It w as found that NCM2 still maintains the original P2 structure after 20 % Co doping, but the pure material NM show ed (022) char acteristic peak of P2'. The same re sult has also been confirmed in the resear ch of o ther Fig. 1. Schematic illustration of the preparat ion process of Na 0.67 Co 0.2 Mn 0.8 O 2. C. cheng Fu, J. W ang, Y. Li et al. Therefor e, Co can effectiv ely inhibit the occurrence of P2-P2' phase tran sition, which is conduciv e to structural stability pro viding fa vor able con ditions for fast insertion and e xsertion of Na +. For the sake of comprehending the morphology and structural charact eristics of materials, a series of tests w ere performed to charact erize the material. It can be seen from Fig. 4 a-f that the particles of the thr ee materials are all poly gonal plate-like struc tures, with a particle size of about 1–2 μm, and the thickness of the sheet is within a few nanomete rs. The results are consistent with the XRD test analy sis. The surface of the NM ( Fig. 4 a, d) materia l is not smooth, and the agglomer ation is relati vel y ob vious. In contrast, the surfaces of NCM1 and NCM2 are smoothe r and less agglomerat ed, which are beneficial to augmenting the specific surface area. It is conduciv e to the activ e materia l fully contact with the electrol yte, further accelerating the charge-di scharge re action rat e [34]. In contrast, the particle size of NCM2 is uniform along with the lay er ed structure is more clearl y visible, the surface is smoothe r. The flake materials gather tog ether to form some micropor es, which is in fa vor of the full penetration of the electrol yte. In addition, a single uniform form can re duce the po wdering of the electrode during the charging and discharging proce ss, which makes for the stability of the structure. T o analyze the element distribution in the NCM2 material, a plane scan of the elements w as performed on the NCM2. Fig. 4 g-k are the corresponding distribution diagrams of O, Na Mn, and Co respecti vel y. It can be seen that the distribution of each element is uniform. It can be seen from Fig. 5 a NCM2 presents a flaky structur e, which is consistent with the results of the SEM image. In addition, w e can find that NCM2 is a lay ered structure formed by stacking sheet-like structures. This re sult is consistent with the results ob tained by XRD. Fig. 5 c is a high-resol ution tran smission electron microsc ope (HRTEM) picture. W e calculated the interplanar spacing to be 2.48 Å. Accor ding to the PDF standar d card in XRD (#2 7–075 1), w e know that the correspondin g crystal plane is (1 0 0) plane. By analyzing the structure of the P2 type NCM2 electrode materia l, it is know n that sodium ions diffuse along the two-di mensional plane perpendicular to the (0 02) plane during the charge and discharge proce ss, and the dir ection perpendicular to the (0 02) plane is the (1 0 0) plane, that is, sodium Ions diffuse along the (1 0 0) plane. Fig. 5 d is the electron diffr action pattern performed in the selecte d area of Fig. 4 c. Analy sis of the diffr action spots show s that NCM2 is a he x agon al materia l. In order to further e xplore the composition of element v alence states, the material w as char acterized by XPS measurement. Fig. 6 a show s the measured spectra of the three cathode materials. The peaks of P 2p, Mn 2p, Co 2p, Na 1s, and O 1s can be clearl y detect ed, and there is no binding energy peak of other elements. Co 2p also e xhibits four peaks, two of which are located at 780.22 eV and 795.20 eV are Co 3+, and the other two peaks at 782.33 eV and 79 7. 1 0 eV are Co 4+. In contrast, the cy cle performance of NCM2 is sig nificantly impro ved. This is largel y because of that when the Co doping content is relati vel y enough. Low -state Co ions are doped at the Mn site, which can increase the ratio of Mn 4+ and reduce the Mn 3+ with JahnT eller activity [42]. It can be seen that NFM has a significant voltag e drop at about 1 .75 V relat ed to the Mn 3+ JahnT eller effect with the increase of the number of cy cles, which has a serious impact on the stability of the lattice structur e of the material. After 1 0 0 cy cles, the coulombic efficiency w as 99. 8 %, 99. 3 %, and 98 %, respecti vel y. Co doping impro ves the coulombic efficiency, which is beneficial to the stability of the structure and makes the insertion and deinter calation of sodium ions smoothl y [43]. In terms of electroc hemistry and structural rev ersibility, the high-rat e charge-discharg e cy cle performance in the voltag e rang e of 1 .5–4.0 V has been further studied. At the end of the discharge, the incorporation of low -priced and high-spin Co 2+ makes the a ver age combined state of Mn slightl y higher than the level of 3 +, which can w ell inhibit the JahnT eller effect and benefit the stability of the structur e [4 1 ,4 4]. NCM2 has e x cellent rat e performance and higher re versibility. The influence of different Co content on the electrode charge tran sfer kinetics is studied by the A C impedance test (EIS). In Fig. 8 g, the diagram is composed of two semicircles, including diagonal lines in the high-freq uency re gion and the lo w-fr eq uency region. The high-freq uency region of the real axis inter cept repr esents the im pedance of ohmic resistance and the solution re sistance, called R s. The mid-freq uency semicir cle repr esents the charge transfer im pedance, called R ct pedance of ohmic resistance and the solution re sistance, called R s. The mid-freq uency semicir cle repr esents the charge transfer im pedance, called R ct, which is caused by the interface betwee n the electrol yte and the electrode. The low -freq uency obliq ue line re presen ts the impedance of sodium ion diffusion in the electrode, which is called W arburg impedance. Har d carbon is considered to be the most pr omising electrode material for sodium-ion batteries on account of its high sodium stor age capacity and low sodium stor age pot ential. As shown in Fig. 1 0 a, in order to verify the practicability of the NCM2 electrode material for full cell, NCM2 w as used as the cathode material, and hard carbon w as used as the anode material in a mass ratio of 1:1 .2 to match the full cell (NNC M//HC). In orde r to pr obe into the effect of Co doping on the density of states of NM, First-principles calculation w as performed. As shown in Fig. S1, NM and NCM2 straddle both sides of the Fe rmi leve l, in dicating that materials ha ve been eq uipped with fa vor able metallic properties. The ob vious band gap can be observed in NM, but the band gap is almost non-e xistent after Co doping, indicating that the electronic conductivity of the material is enhanced after Co doping [48]. In addition, manganese ions in NM e xist in a mix ed configuration of Mn 3+ and Mn 4+, but Mn 3+ occupies the ma jority. While the proportion of Mn 4+ (t 2 g 3 -eg 0 ) increased after Co doping. It is well known that un paired electron s Mn 3+ has strong JahnT eller activ ity, which can lead to lattice structure distortion and charge orde ring, thus limiting the inter calation and deinter calation of Na +. Therefor e, we conclude that the distortion of the JahnT eller effect for Mn 3+ can be effectiv el y wea kened by Co doping. A ccording to the theoret ical specific capacity formula ( =Q nF M ), NCM2 corr esponds to 0.58 sodium re lease when charged to 4.0 V. In order to more fully comprehen d the electron beha vior during char ging and discharging, the PDOS are plot ted in Fig. 1 1 a-l. When Na is emigrat ed (Na 0.5 ), the spin orbits of Mn and Co on eg graduall y mov e from the left to the right side of the Fe rmi level. The shif t indicates that Mn 3+ (t 2g 3 -eg1) is o xidized to Mn 4+ (t 2 g 3 -eg 0 ) combined with Co 2+ is o xidized to Co 3+, and the charge compensation is pr ovided by Co and Mn tog ether in this process. When charging to Na 0.34, the charge compensation of Mn ha ve accomplished, and Co continues to play the compensation role until the end of charging. The electronic structur e w as further inv estigated and found that the strong cov a lency between Co t 2 g and O 2p forms an electron -deficient state or "hole" in the O 2p orbital, which is beneficial to inhibit the loss of o xy gen, ther eby impro ving the structural stability [50]. T o further clarify the reason for the e x cellent rat e performance of NCM2. Na + diffusion of materials w as inv estigated by First principles calcula tions using the NEB method. The correspondin g Na + migration bar riers of NM and NCM2 are shown in Fig. 1 1 m and Fig. 1 1 n show s the Na + diffusion paths. Theoretical calculations show ed that the e x cessi ve migrat ion barrier of Na + in NM is about 1 .2 1 eV, which is much higher than that of NCM2 (0.58 eV). The results make clear that the Co-doping modification can pr omot e the diffusion of Na + and pro vide facile ion diffusion channels [5 1]. 4. Conclusions In summary, lay ered Na 0.67 Co 0.2 Mn 0.8 O 2 for SIBs w as successfull y prepar ed thr ough the h ydr othermal method. Among the man y P2 lay ered materials, w e chose the low -cost Mn base tran sition metal Fig. 1 1. The electrochemical stability of Na 0.67 MnO 2 is poor, which is mainly for the sake of Na+ / v acancy along with the slip of the MO 2 lay er during the process of sodium ion de-inter calation, causing the irr eversible phase transition. The po sitiv e effects of Co doping on Na 0.67 MnO 2 wer e comprehensi vel y charact erized by the morphology, crystal structur e, and charge sto rag e mechanism. Co doping at the Mn site increases the proport ion of Mn 4+ and JahnT eller effect distortion is effectiv ely suppressed pro ven by DFT and XPS tests. Na 0.67 Co 0.2 Mn 0.8 O 2 still has 88. 7 % capacity ret ention rat e after 20 0 cy cles at 2 C and the re versibility and cy cling stability of the material ha ve been significantly im pro ved pro ved by tests. Co-doping modification can achieve pre ferabl y cy cle stability for sodium ion batt eries.
